<h1>The Hardest Boulder Problems in the World</h1>
<p><img data-pin-title="The Hardest Boulder Problems in the World (2019 Update)" class="simple-border alignright wp-image-5997 size-medium" src="https://www.99boulders.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/Map-of-the-world-300x213.jpg" alt="A map of the world" width="300" height="213" /><em><strong>Last updated:</strong> March 5, 2019. If you notice any omissions, broken links, or other errors, leave a comment below letting us know.</em></p>
<p>V16 (8C+) boulder problems are finally starting to become more common. There are now 12 problems with proposed or consensus grades of V16.</p>
<p><em>Creature from the Black Lagoon</em> has now been sent by six climbers, five of whom suggested a grade of V16, further solidifying the bloc&#8217;s spot in bouldering history as the first consensus V16 boulder problem.</p>
<p>What follows is a sortable list of all the hardest boulder problems in the world. The lower cutoff grade is V15, or 8C on the <a href="https://www.99boulders.com/bouldering-grades" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Font Scale</a>. Many of the problems do not yet have a consensus grade, so I came up with <a href="#list-criteria">a formulaic way</a> to assign one to each based off the existing grade suggestions.</p>
<p>I&#8217;ve tried my best to be as comprehensive as possible with this list. However, I&#8217;m still human. If I&#8217;ve made any mistakes or left off any problems or people you think should be added, let me know in the comments and I&#8217;ll take a look at it during the next update.</p>
<h3>Highlights from the Latest Update</h3>
<ul>
<li><strong>World&#8217;s second V17:</strong> <em>No Kpote Only</em> became the second boulder problem ever to receive a proposed grade of V17 (9A) after barefoot climber Charles Albert got the FA in December 2018.</li>
<li><strong>Even more V16s:</strong> In this latest update alone we added five boulder problems with proposed grades of V16 (8C+): <em>Box Therapy</em>, <em>Hypothèse assis</em>, <em>Off the Wagon Sit</em>, <em>Poison the Well</em>, and <em>Sleepwalker</em>.</li>
</ul>

<h3>The World&#8217;s Current Hardest Boulder Problem</h3>
<p>Based solely on grade, <strong>the title of world&#8217;s hardest boulder problem is currently shared by two problems: <em>Burden of Dreams</em> and <em>No Kpote Only</em>. Both are currently graded V17 (9A).</strong></p>
<p>Both problems have only one ascent. Nalle Hukkataival sent <em>Burden of Dreams</em> in October 2016, making it the first problem ever to receive a proposed grade of V17 (9A). Charles Albert sent <em>No Kpote Only</em> in December 2018.</p>
<p><strong>» MORE:</strong> <a href="https://www.99boulders.com/hardest-sport-climbs" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">The Hardest Sport Climbs in the World</a></p>
<h3 id="list-criteria">List Criteria &amp; Grading Guidelines</h3>
<ul>
<li><strong>The grade had to be V15 (8C) or higher.</strong> In other words, problems graded V14/V15 (8B+/8C) and lower were left off the list. For the remainder of the article, I will refer to problems graded V15 (8C) or higher as &#8220;hard&#8221; problems.</li>
<li><strong>For problems with no consensus grade, I averaged the <a href="https://www.99boulders.com/bouldering-grades" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">V Scale translation</a> of the grade suggestions. If the average had a remainder less than ⅓, I rounded down. If the average had a remainder between ⅓ and ⅔, I treated it as having a slash grade. If the average had a remainder above ⅔, I rounded up. I also averaged slash grades: V14/V15 was treated as 14.5, for instance.</strong> For example, let&#8217;s consider the problem <em>Khoikhoi</em>. Currently, three climbers have sent it. Jimmy Webb proposed a grade of V14 (8B+). Nalle Hukkataival and Shawn Raboutou both proposed a grade of V15 (8C). I averaged the V Scale translation of these grades (14, 15, 15) to get 14⅔. Since the remainder is ⅔, I treated <em>Khoikhoi</em> as having a slash grade of V14/V15 (8B+/8C) and thus left it off the list. If one more climber were to send it and propose a grade of V15 &#8212; or if Jimmy Webb were to bump his suggestion up to V15 &#8212; I would add it.</li>
<li><strong>I did not take into account anything other than the proposed grades.</strong> Some climbers are known for grading hard. Some problems are considered soft for their grade. Some problems on this list could be considered traverses. I didn’t consider any of this. I respected each climber&#8217;s suggestion and just considered the proposed grade(s).</li>
</ul>
<h2>Who Is the Best Boulderer Ever?</h2>
<p><img data-pin-title="The Hardest Boulder Problems in the World (2019 Update)" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-3090" src="https://www.99boulders.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/best-ever.png" alt="Who is the best boulderer ever?" width="750" height="100" srcset="https://www.99boulders.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/best-ever-300x40.png 300w, https://www.99boulders.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/best-ever.png 750w" sizes="(max-width: 750px) 100vw, 750px" /><br />
Here are two charts based on the data in the above list showing who has sent the most hard boulder problems and who has racked up the most hard boulder first ascents (FAs).</p>
<div id="visualizer-11773-1458909802"class="visualizer-front  visualizer-front-11773"></div><!-- Not showing structured data for chart 11773 because description is empty -->
<div id="visualizer-11775-1331056351"class="visualizer-front  visualizer-front-11775"></div><!-- Not showing structured data for chart 11775 because description is empty -->
<p>Daniel Woods has the most hard boulder sends and second most hard boulder FAs. Dai Koyamada has the most hard boulder FAs and second most hard boulder sends. Nalle Hukkataival is third in both categories and has the first and only ascent of the world&#8217;s first proposed V17 (9A). One could make the case for any of them as the world&#8217;s best boulderer.</p>
<p>Sheer volume of hard sends and FAs is admittedly not the only way to assess a boulderer&#8217;s ability. At the very least, these three are the most prolific outdoor boulderers of their time.</p>
<p><strong>» MORE:</strong> <a href="https://www.99boulders.com/hardest-trad-climbs" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">The Hardest Trad Climbs in the World</a></p>
<h2 id="grade-chasing">Grade-Chasing</h2>
<div id="visualizer-14925-1980743044"class="visualizer-front  visualizer-front-14925"></div><!-- Not showing structured data for chart 14925 because description is empty -->
<p>The first boulder problem to ever receive a suggested grade of V15 (8C) was <em>Dreamtime</em>, which Fred Nicole put up in 2000. <em>Dreamtime</em> has since been downgraded, but in 2002 Nicole climbed <em>Black Eagle SD</em> and <em>Monkey Wedding</em> which both currently stand as consensus V15s.</p>
<p>Put another way, it took just two years from the time the V15 grade was first proposed for a problem to be put up whose V15 grade would hold after multiple repeats.</p>
<p>(There is another V15 that was put up before <em>Black Eagle SD</em> and <em>Monkey Wedding</em>. But the problem, <em>Gossip</em>, has only two grade suggestions and is therefore still at risk of being downgraded.)</p>
<p>The story is different for the V16 (8C+) grade. The first problem with a proposed grade of V16 appears to have been <em>Tonino &#8217;78</em>, first sent by Mauro Calibani in 2004. It wasn&#8217;t until 12 years later, in 2016, that Daniel Woods would put up <em>Creature from the Black Lagoon</em>, the world&#8217;s first consensus V16.</p>
<p>Assuming <em>Creature from the Black Lagoon&#8217;s</em> grade continues to withstand the test of time, it has taken a decade longer for the V16 grade to go from suggestion to consensus than it did V15. That&#8217;s a staggering, and intriguing, difference.</p>
<div id="visualizer-14934-109104234"class="visualizer-front  visualizer-front-14934"></div><!-- Not showing structured data for chart 14934 because description is empty -->
<p>Interestingly, well over one hundred different climbers have climbed a V15 (8C) problem. Then comes quite a drop-off. Only 13 have climbed a V15/V16 (8C/8C+). 13 have also climbed a V16 (8C+). Just two have climbed a V17 (9A).</p>
<p>Downgrading of V16 problems is still quite common. For example, in 2016 Alberto Rocasolano proposed a grade of V16 for <em>La teoría del todo</em> after getting the first ascent. A few months later Rubén Díaz Torres got the second ascent and proposed a grade of V15. Then in 2018 Jonatan Flor Vazquez claimed the third ascent and proposed a grade of V14.</p>
<p>It&#8217;s easy to wonder what&#8217;s going on. <em>Why all the downgrading? Shouldn&#8217;t there be more V16s?</em></p>
<p>Sometimes new beta gets found that makes a problem easier. But that doesn&#8217;t explain all cases. Nalle wrote <a href="https://nalle-hukkataival.blogspot.com/2010/03/bouldering-grades-everything-is-average.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">a blog post</a> way back in 2010 detailing his thoughts on why this apparent stalling of grade progression happened.</p>
<p>Though V16 sends have remained elusive, as I updated this article throughout 2017 and 2018 I sensed that start to change. Sure, downgrading still happens regularly, but top climbers are proposing V16s more and more often.</p>
<p>Of course, two proposed V17s (9As) also exist. Nalle climbed <em>Burden of Dreams</em> in October 2016, just a month after Woods climbed <em>Creature from the Black Lagoon</em>. More recently, Charles Albert climbed <em>No Kpote Only</em>.</p>
<p>Both problems have yet to see any repeats. If history is any indicator, it&#8217;s highly possible that both will be downgraded by future ascensionists. As for how long it&#8217;ll take for a consensus V17 to emerge…well, that&#8217;s anyone&#8217;s guess.</p>
<h2>Where in the World Are the Hardest Boulder Problems?</h2>
<p>There&#8217;s a map for that:</p>
<div id="visualizer-11767-395615931"class="visualizer-front  visualizer-front-11767"></div><!-- Not showing structured data for chart 11767 because title is empty -->
<p>And a chart:</p>
<div id="visualizer-11769-1310870511"class="visualizer-front  visualizer-front-11769"></div><!-- Not showing structured data for chart 11769 because description is empty -->
<p>Currently, only 21 countries are home to a hard boulder problem. And it&#8217;s quite incredible to realize:</p>
<ul>
<li>14 of those countries are in Europe</li>
<li>There is only one country from Africa and South America on the list: South Africa and Brazil, respectively</li>
<li>There are only two hard boulder problems in all of mainland Asia: <em>Hymn</em> and <em>Eternal Sunshine</em>, both located in South Korea. (<em>Whiplash</em> is located in the European part of Russia.)</li>
</ul>
<p>Bouldering&#8217;s global potential remains largely untapped. As the sport matures one can only imagine all the new crags and problems that will arise.</p>
<h2>When to Project vs. When to Train, Backed by Data</h2>
<p><img data-pin-title="The Hardest Boulder Problems in the World (2019 Update)" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-3093" src="https://www.99boulders.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/training.png" alt="When to project vs. when to train" width="750" height="100" srcset="https://www.99boulders.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/training-300x40.png 300w, https://www.99boulders.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/training.png 750w" sizes="(max-width: 750px) 100vw, 750px" /><br />
Finally, for fun I charted the ascents of all the hard boulder problems by month for both the northern and southern hemispheres.</p>
<div id="visualizer-11761-1842500881"class="visualizer-front  visualizer-front-11761"></div><!-- Not showing structured data for chart 11761 because description is empty -->
<div id="visualizer-11762-1863988909"class="visualizer-front  visualizer-front-11762"></div><!-- Not showing structured data for chart 11762 because description is empty -->
<p>Most of the hard boulder sends in both hemispheres came in the coldest months of the year. At the very least, these charts can give you some insight on when to tackle your projects and when to focus on training.</p>
<p><em>I have to give a special shout-out to <a href="http://www.8a.nu/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">8a.nu</a> and <a href="http://www.hardclimbs.info/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">HardClimbs.info</a>. Both sites were instrumental in putting together this article. It wouldn&#8217;t exist without these incredible resources.</em></p>
